This Student Internship Agreement (the "Agreement") has been entered into as of May 20th. 2025 by and between 
Riverhead Police Department with its principal place of business at 210 Howell Ave, Riverhead, NY 11901 and THE 
UNIVERSITY OF RHODE ISLAND, a public institution of higher education, acting by and through its Center for 
Career and Experiential Education, located at Roosevelt Hall, 90 Lower College Road, Kingston, RI 02881 (the 
"University"). 
9.19.a
Packet Pg. 106
Attachment: Student Internship Agreement  (2025-260 : Authorizes the Chief of Police to Execute a Student Intern Agreement)
• WHEREAS, the University has established programming to give students experiential learning opportunities in various 
community organizations which complement their chosen disciplines, and 
WHEREAS, Host operates and/or controls the organization or facilities known as Riverhead Police Department 
located in/at 210 Howell Ave. Riverhead, NY 11901 the "Organization") [Note: The Host-controlled organization 
and location listed here may be the same as, or different than, the Host's official name and address listed above]; and 
WHEREAS, the parties agree that the development of an experiential learning internship (the "Program") whereby one 
or more of the University's students (each, an "Intern") can obtain practical experience in Organization's setting would 
benefit the University, the Interns and Internship Host, all of which will ultimately provide improved services to the 
community. 
NOW THEREFORE, in consideration of the mutual benefits accruing to the parties under this Agreement, and other 
good and valuable consideration, the receipt and sufficiency of which is hereby acknowledged, it is agreed as 
follows. 
1. THE PROGRAM 
The parties have designed the Program described in "Exhibit A" (which is attached hereto and incorporated herein) to 
allow the Intern(s) to obtain practical experience in Organization's operations. During the Internship, the student will 
participate in the specific Program related activities described in "Exhibit A". 
2. TERM; TERMINATION 
This Agreement will commence on the Effective Date and shall continue up to and including, (the "Term"). 
Notwithstanding the foregoing, at any time during the Term, either party may terminate this Agreement upon written 
notice to the other, such termination to be effective at the conclusion of the then current academic semester or term. 
3. HOST RESPONSIBILITIES 
3.1 General Duty of Instruction and Supervision. The Host agrees to assume responsibility for the direction, oversight 
and supervision of the Intern's experiential learning and supervised work experiences (which are designed and conducted 
in general accordance with the Intern's approved Learning Agreement referenced below) occurring while the Intern 
participates in the program and Host's designated Internship location. Without limiting the generality of the foregoing, 
the Host shall provide reasonable supervision and feedback to each Intern and to the University, including verifying in 
writing all hours and dates worked by an Intern. Host will also promptly report to the University the unsatisfactory 
progress (including without limitation unexcused absences) of any Intern. 
3.2 Care of Host's Clients/Customers. Host will remain responsible at all times for the care of, and the provision of 
services to, its clients, customers, patients, students, as the case may be. In the event that Intern will participate in the 
provision of services that are properly only done by (or legally required to only be done by) the Host's qualified 
employees, the Intern's participation in the provision of those services shall always (a) be strictly limited to what is 
permitted by law and by the Host's policies, and (b) be under the direct control, direction and supervision of the Host's 
qualified employees. 
3.3 Staffing. Host will maintain at least its normal staffing levels while Interns are present at an Organization. In no event 
will an Intern be expected or allowed to perform services in lieu of staff employees. 
3.4 Host's Standards. Host will supply any of Host's applicable standards, procedures and code of ethics to Intern, to 
9.19.a
Packet Pg. 107
Attachment: Student Internship Agreement  (2025-260 : Authorizes the Chief of Police to Execute a Student Intern Agreement)
alldw the Intern to acquaint themselves with them. 
* 3.5 Licenses, Certifications, Approvals, Training and Other Requirements. The Host will ensure that it obtains and/or 
assists or arranges for the Intern to obtain, any and all necessary licenses, certifications, and approvals (including any 
required or appropriate background checks or health assessments) that are required by applicable laws or the Host's 
policies, in order to allow the Intern to participate in the Program. The Host will also ensure that the Intern receives and 
completes all necessary and/or appropriate training and education that the Intern requires in order to legally, safely, 
successfully and appropriately participate in the Program. 
3.6 Host's Program Coordinator and Field Supervisors. Host shall designate one of its employees to serve as the "Host 
Program Coordinator" who shall serve as the primary responsible liaison to the University responsible for all program 
related communication and coordination with the University. The Host shall also designate any additional "Field 
Supervisors" (in addition to the Host Program Coordinator who may be the sole Field Supervisor for the program as 
well) who will supervise and educate the Intern during the Program. The University must approve the Host Program 
Coordinator and any additional Field Supervisors, but its approval of those individuals will not be unreasonably 
withheld. The Host's Program Coordinator shall be listed in the Program Description attached as Exhibit A, and shall 
also be required to indicate his/her understanding of, and assent to, the terms of this Agreement (including Exhibit A) by 
his/her signature at the end of this Agreement. 
3.7 Learning Outcomes Agreement. The Host, through its Host Program Coordinator, will work with the designated 
University Program Coordinator and the Intern to develop a written "Learning Outcomes Agreement" which is intended 
to give structure to the internship by listing specific goals for student educational outcomes and field learning 
experiences. It is expected that the Intern, the University Program Coordinator, and the Host Program Coordinator will 
all approve in writing the Learning Outcomes Agreement prior to the commencement of the internship. The Learning 
Outcomes Agreement may be modified thereafter only with the approval of those same three parties. 3.8 Intern 
Placement. Accept students for placement as Interns at Host, the exact number to be decided annually by Host and 
University. Limited to a maximum of 10 students from the same major in a state other than Rhode Island, as required by 
law. 
3.9 Non-Discrimination. Provide a work/learning environment for students that is without discrimination based on race, 
color, national origin, age, sex, religion, disability, veteran status, sexual orientation or marital status. 
3.10 Educational Appropriateness. Provide educationally sound Internships for students. 
3.11 Duties and Capacities of Field Supervisors. Assure that each Field Supervisor has adequate time within his/her 
work schedule to: 
• Meet the educational needs of the student, including: orientation to the company and its services, development of 
learning opportunities which include depth and variety, and preparation for at least weekly conferences with 
each student; 
• Communicate with the University Program Coordinator at periodic intervals to discuss learning opportunity and 
student performance 
• Complete a midterm and final evaluation as provided by and required by University, including a comprehensive 
evaluation of each student's performance at the end of that student's placement with Host. 
3.12 Student Intern Access to Facilities and Resources. Provide students with: 
• Sufficient work space, including a desk for each student in an area sufficiently private for carrying on his/her 
independent work and activity; 
• Convenient access to a telephone; 
• Office supplies, as needed, in the performance of responsibilities; 
• Access to client and Host's records appropriate to the student's learning experience. 
3.13 Parking. Provide adequate parking for students during duty periods, and, when resources allow, provide either 
9.19.a
Packet Pg. 108
Attachment: Student Internship Agreement  (2025-260 : Authorizes the Chief of Police to Execute a Student Intern Agreement)
trarsportation or reimbursement of approved travel if students must travel on behalf of clients. 3.14 General Host 
• Responsibility for Student Work. Supervise and assume responsibility for the students Intern's work with Host. 
3.15 Intern Safety and Health. Provide a safe work/learning environment for students, including first aid and 
emergency medical care and referral to an appropriate health care provider if needed. Host will inform students of any 
health and/or safety issues or concerns in the Internship location prior to the start of the internship. 
4. UNIVERSITY RESPONSIBILITIES 
4.1 Qualification of Interns. The University shall ensure, through qualified university staff and curriculum that each 
Intern is adequately prepared to benefit from his or her placement in the Program. An Intern's preparedness shall be 
measured by (i) academic performance indicating an ability to understand what the Intern will observe and perform 
while participating in the Program, (ii) an appreciation of the nature and gravity of the work Intern will observe and 
perform, and (iii) the Intern's disposition and conduct as appropriate for the setting. Prior to the commencement of their 
Internship, the University will also ensure that all Interns involved in the Program become familiar with and are 
instructed that they must adhere to all applicable legal requirements as well as Host's standards, procedures and code of 
ethics. 
4.2 General Obligations to Host. Consider the needs and recommendations of Host in all matters concerning its field 
instruction program; 
4.3 University Program Coordinator. The University will appoint one (1) university staff member to serve as the 
educational coordinator for the Program (the "University Program Coordinator"). The University Program Coordinator 
will be responsible for the overall management of the Intern's educational experience while participating in the Program. 
The University Program Coordinator shall be listed in the Program Description attached as Exhibit A and shall also be 
required to indicate his/her understanding of, and assent to, the terms of this Agreement (including Exhibit A) by his/her 
signature at the end of this Agreement. The University Program Coordinator shall also: 
• Serve as principal liaison between University and Host including appropriate communication with University's 
Director of Experiential Education; 
• Be reasonably available to the Host's Program Coordinator and Field Supervisors for consultation when 
requested; and 
• Share with the Field Supervisors knowledge of the educational program of University. 
4.4 Learning Outcomes Agreement. Work with students to prepare a "Learning Outcomes Agreement" that will give 
structure to the internship experience by listing goals for student educational outcomes and field learning experiences. 
It is expected that the Student Intern, the University Program Coordinator and the Host Program Coordinator will all 
agree in writing to the learning outcomes agreement prior to the midterm. 
4.5 Approval of Host Personnel. Review and accept where appropriate the Host's recommendations for the Host Program 
Coordinator and any additional Field Supervisors. 
4.6 Academic Oversight. Administer the academic aspects of the Program, including decisions which affect the progress of 
the student, such as grades, credits, and field hours. 
5. INTERN RESPONSIBILITIES 
At all times while participating in the Program at the Organization, all Interns shall adhere to Host's workplace policies, 
rules and regulations, including those relating to the use of alcohol and other drugs, weapons, dress code, timeliness, and 
9.19.a
Packet Pg. 109
Attachment: Student Internship Agreement  (2025-260 : Authorizes the Chief of Police to Execute a Student Intern Agreement)
professional conduct; maintain good standing at the University, and maintain accurate, daily log sheets of all hours 
- worked. Host will familiarize Interns with Host's standards, procedures and code of ethics. 
6. FERPA COMPLIANCE 
The parties recognize that they are bound to comply with the Family Educational Rights and Privacy Act (Buckley 
Amendment) in their handling of educational records of students enrolled in their programs. It is also understood and 
recognized that employees and agents of each party will need to have access to the educational records maintained by the 
other party in properly administering their duties and obligations under this Agreement and to the individual students. It 
is agreed that each party shall thoroughly orient their employees and agents with regard to their respective obligations 
under the Family Educational Rights and Privacy Act and shall maintain their practices in strict accordance with the 
requirements of that act. Unless required by judicial or regulatory authority, neither party shall be permitted to authorize 
and further disclose the educational records of the other party to persons or entities not a party to this Agreement without 
first having received permission of the other party and having obtained assurances that the other party has fully complied 
with the provisions of the Family Educational Rights and Privacy Act. Any permitted disclosure to persons or entities not 
a party to this Agreement shall be under the condition that no further disclosure by such party shall be permitted. Each 
party agrees to save, indemnify and hold harmless the other party and their officers, employees and agents from any 
liability, damages, claims actions, causes of actions, demands, judgments or awards of whatsoever kind or nature, arising 
out of any failure by the other party or its officers, employees or agents to abide by the Family Educational Rights and 
Privacy Act or its implementing regulations. 
7. INSURANCE and INDEMNIFICATION 
7.1 Student Liability Insurance. University shall maintain a general liability insurance policy covering its students in the 
amounts of $1,000,000.00 per incident and $3,000,000.00 in the annual aggregate. A copy of the policy or certificate will 
be provided upon request. 
7.2 Host General Liability Insurance. The Host shall provide a current and up-to-date certificate of General Liability 
Insurance to the University Program Coordinator, showing coverage in the amounts of $1,000,000.00 per incident and 
$3,000,000.00 in the annual aggregate. This requirement may be waived, or modified as appropriate, in the exclusive 
discretion of the University, on a case by case basis, such as when the Host is public/governmental entity. 
7.3 Indemnification. Each party shall defend and indemnify the other party (and its governing boards and board members, 
directors, officers, employees, students, agents and representatives) from and against all claims and resulting liabilities 
and damages, resulting from the negligence or wrongful conduct of the indemnifying party and/or its employees, 
students, agents and representatives. This requirement may be waived, or modified as appropriate, in the exclusive 
discretion of the University, on a case by case basis, such as when the Host is public/governmental entity. 
8. CONFIDENTIALITY 
8.1 Definition. Each party may in some cases (at the discretion of the disclosing party, when it is considered necessary or 
appropriate to help ensure the success of the internship arrangement) be given access to the other party's confidential and 
proprietary information. "Confidential Information" shall mean material or information proprietary to either party or 
designated as Confidential Information by such party and not generally known by third parties. Confidential Information 
includes, but is not limited to, the following types of information and other information of a similar nature (whether or 
not reduced to writing): the existence and terms of this Agreement; patient, customer, employee and student records, 
including names, addresses, telephone numbers, and other information related to patients, customers, employees, and 
students; marketing techniques and materials; marketing and development plans and procedures; and financial 
9.19.a
Packet Pg. 110
Attachment: Student Internship Agreement  (2025-260 : Authorizes the Chief of Police to Execute a Student Intern Agreement)
infdrmation, all of which it considers trade secret. 
8.2 Duty to Protect. Each party will protect the other party's Confidential Information and will only disclose Confidential 
Information to persons who have a "need to know" the Confidential Information to provide services under this 
Agreement. Each Party will apprise said persons of the confidentiality obligations and ensure that they comply with the 
terms of this 
Agreement. 
8.3 Exclusions. Confidential Information will not include information which: (a) is or becomes available to the general 
public through no fault of the party receiving the Confidential Information (the "Recipient"); (b) is independently 
developed by the Recipient as evidenced by Recipient's own records; (c) is rightfully received by the Recipient from a 
third party without a duty of confidentiality; (d) is required to be disclosed by court order or operation of law; or 
(e) is required to be disclosed under the provisions of Rhode island's public records laws. Before disclosing any 
Confidential Information under a court order or operation of law, the Recipient shall provide the other party (the "Injured 
Party") reasonable notice and the opportunity to object to or limit such disclosure. 
8.4 Client/Customer Records. The University acknowledges and agrees that all client or customer records of Host shall be 
and remain the property of and in the custody of Host. Upon termination of this Agreement, the University and its faculty 
and students shall neither retain nor have access to any client or customer records obtained under this Agreement. 
8.5 Survival. The rights and obligations of this Article shall survive the expiration or sooner termination of this 
Agreement. 
9. EMPLOYMENT PRACTICES 
9.1 Recordkeeping. Each party's respective employment, healthcare and record keeping practices shall conform to all 
federal, state and local statutes, ordinances, and rules and regulations. 
9.2 Termination of Interns. Host shall have the right to terminate, at any time, with or without notice, the training of any 
Intern whose performance is unsatisfactory or whose characteristics and activities are detrimental to Host's business or 
organizational activity. Termination of a student must be followed with a written communication to the University 
Program Coordinator, including a statement of facts describing the Intern's unacceptable conduct that resulted in such 
termination. 
9.3 No Compensation. The parties understand and agree that neither party, nor any Intern, will be entitled to 
compensation hereunder for its participation in the Program. No Intern will be considered an employee of either the 
University or Host as a result of participation in the Program, and neither the University nor Host will be responsible for 
Worker's Compensation coverage with respect to any Intern. 
10. MISCELLANEOUS 
10.1 Force Majeure. Neither party shall be responsible for any failure to perform or delay in performing any of its 
obligations under this Agreement where and to the extent that such failure or delay results from causes outside the 
reasonable control of the party. Such causes shall include, without limitation, Acts of God or of the public enemy, acts of 
the government in either its sovereign or contractual capacity, fires, floods, epidemics, quarantine restrictions, freight 
embargoes, civil commotion, or the like. Notwithstanding the above, strikes and labor disputes shall not constitute an 
excusable delay for either party under this Agreement. The Agreement may be terminated without penalty by the party

whose performance has not been affected if nonperformance continues for more than thirty (30) days. 
10.2 Headings, Counterparts. Headings used in this Agreement are for reference purposes only and shall not be used to 
modify the meaning of the terms and conditions of this Agreement. This Agreement may be executed in two or more 
counterparts each of which shall be deemed an original, but all of which together shall constitute one and the same 
instrument. 
10.3 Modification of Agreement. This Agreement shall not be modified or amended except by a written document 
executed by an authorized representative of each party. 
10.4 Severability. If any provision contained in this Agreement is held invalid, illegal, or unenforceable, then this 
Agreement will be construed as if such provision had never been contained herein. 
10.5 Compliance with Laws. The parties will comply with all applicable laws, ordinances, rules, and regulations 
governing their respective duties or responsibilities under this Agreement. University is a public body of the State of 
Rhode Island and is subject to the Rhode Island Access to Public Records Act. 
10.6 li ldependent Contractor. The parties hereto are independent contractors and have no authority to act for the other 
party except as expressly provided in this Agreement. Nothing herein shall be deemed to create any association, 
partnership, joint venture or agency relationship between the University and Host. This Agreement shall not be construed 
under any circumstance to confer any rights or privileges on any third parties, and neither Host nor the University shall 
be under any obligation to any third party by reason of this Agreement or any term thereof. 
10.7 Publicity. Neither party will use the name(s), trademark(s) or trade name(s), whether registered or not, of the other 
party in publicity or press releases or advertising or in any manner, including customer lists, without that party's prior 
written consent. 
10.8 Notices. All notices under this Agreement (excluding routine communications) shall be personally delivered or sent 
by express, certified or registered mail, return receipt requested, to:

10.9 Conduct. At all times while present at an Organization, the University and its employees and students (including the 
Interns) will comply with all applicable Host policies including without limitation: (i) no smoking; (ii) drug-free 
environment; (iii) dress code; (iv) non-harassment; (v) all safety and security policies (including a prohibition against 
weapons), (vi) computer security and use policies; (vii) HIPAA compliance; and (viii) employee code of conduct. 
10.10 Non-Assignment. Neither party may assign or subcontract its duties or responsibilities under this Agreement 
without the prior written approval of the other party. 
10.11 Non-Waiver. No waiver of any breach of any provision of this Agreement shall constitute a waiver of any prior, 
concurrent or subsequent breach of such provision or any other provisions hereof and no waiver shall be effective unless 
made in writing. 
10.12 Entire Agreement. This Agreement constitutes the entire agreement between the parties and any prior understanding 
regarding the same subject matter will not be binding except to the extent incorporated in this Agreement. 
10.13 Governing Law. This agreement shall be governed by the laws of the state of Rhode Island.

Attachment: Student Internship Agreement  (2025-260 : Authorizes the Chief of Police to Execute a Student Intern Agreement)
Position Title: Intern 
Date 1/22/2025 
"EXHIBIT A" 
Program Description 
Being an intern is an excellent way to get firsthand experience in any future career that a student is 
interested in. The Riverhead Police Department allows interns to get an inside look at a career in Law 
Enforcement and how our Police Department runs on a daily basis. They will be able to see firsthand 
some of the different roles ie; Patrol, Detectives, Crime Control, Harbor Master and the COPE Unit. The 
intern will be able to shadow these roles and get a better idea of what a typical workday looks like. We 
also work closely with our Justice Court that allows interns to sit in on Jury Trials so they can get a full 
picture of Law and Order. There is also the other side of the department that houses our Public Safety 
Dispatchers, IT Department and Clerical aides. These roles are also vital to the daily function of our 
Police Department and it would be beneficial to shadow them for a day as well. Our main goal is to 
provide as many opportunities as we can to give our interns an in-depth picture of what a career in law 
enforcement entails. We hope this will assist them in the future when deciding their own career path.

TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
 
TB Resolution 2025-262 
 
RATIFIES THE SETTLEMENT OF LEGAL ACTION AGAINST RIVERHEAD NY 
PROPERTIES LLC 
 
Councilman Rothwell offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilman Kern 
 
WHEREAS, a legal action was commenced in the name of the Town of Riverhead 
against Riverhead NY Properties LLC, the owner of the property known and designated 
as 911 Ostrander Avenue, Riverhead, New York, in the Supreme Court of the State of 
New York, County of Suffolk under Index Number 630347/2023, to enjoin the use and 
occupancy of said property; and 
WHEREAS, the parties have reached a settlement of that legal action inclusive of all 
costs, expenses and interest; and 
WHEREAS, in light of the costs attendant to proceeding to a trial together with the 
uncertainties of litigation, the Town Attorney’s Office demanded, and received, certain terms 
of settlement, including civil penalties payable to the Town in the sum of $12,000.00. 
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Town Board of the Town of 
Riverhead be and hereby accepts and ratifies the settlement reached regarding legal 
action in the name of the Town of Riverhead against Riverhead NY Properties LLC, the 
owner of the property known and designated as 911 Ostrander Avenue, Riverhead, 
New York, in the Supreme Court of the State of New York, County of Suffolk under 
Index Number 630347/2023, to enjoin the use and occupancy of said property; and be it 
further,  
 
 RESOLVED, that the Town Board ratifies authorization for the Office of the Town 
Attorney to enter into a stipulation of settlement on behalf of the Town as well as any other 
documents necessary to effectuate the settlement of the litigation; and it is further,  
 
 RESOLVED, that the Town Clerk is hereby directed to forward  a certified copy of 
this resolution to the Accounting Department and the Office of the Town Attorney ; and be it 
further,  
 
RESOLVED, that all Town Hall Departments may review and obtain a copy of this 
resolution from the electronic storage device and, if needed, a certified copy of same 
may be obtained from the Office of the Town Clerk. 
 
THE VOTE

TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
 
TB Resolution 2025-263 
 
ASSUMES LEAD AGENCY AND ISSUES NEGATIVE DECLARATION PURSUANT 
TO SEQRA FOR TOWN OF RIVERHEAD DOWNTOWN REVITALIZATION 
PROJECTS 
 
Councilman Kern offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilwoman Merrifield 
 
WHEREAS, the Town of Riverhead Town Board and Community Development 
Agency have developed plans for downtown Riverhead to achieve goals previously 
identified by prior studies and significant public involvement and the genera l goals 
identified include eliminating urban blight and revitalizing the downtown region; and 
  
WHEREAS, the overall redevelopment plan encompasses more than 10 acres 
that will experience various degrees of disturbance. The Town Square will be developed 
as an Upper and Lower Town Square, terraced with landscaped public space from Main 
Street and sloping down toward the Peconic River. The proposed developments serve 
to improve public access to the Peconic River and stimulate cultural, recreational, and 
commercial development. The proposed developments are needed to improve the Main 
Street area through increased public awareness of the Riverfront, improved public 
safety, flood attenuation, storm resiliency, historic building preservation and educational 
opportunities within an Urban Renewal Area, with development to be implemented as a 
three (3) phase project: and  
 
WHEREAS, the project description stated herein above supersedes and 
supplements recitation(s) contained within Town Board Resolution 2024 -982, adopted 
December 23, 2024 and more specifically conforms to the description provided within 
the Full Environmental Assessment Form Part 1 Narrative; and 
 
 WHEREAS, by Resolution 2024 -982 the Town Board of the Town of Riverhead 
classified the action as Type 1 p ursuant to SEQRA, and initiated Coordinated Review 
amongst involved agencies listed within Resolution 2024-982; and     
 
WHEREAS, no objections were raised to the Town Board’s Lead Agency request 
during the mandatory 30-day Lead Agency Coordination period with all correspondence 
received contained within and reflected in the SEQRA record; and 
 
WHEREAS, the Riverhead Town Board has considered the SEQRA record to 
date, including Part 1 of the Full Environmental Assessment Form (FEAF), and its 
supplemental Narrative and Appendices dated December 17, 2024 prepared by Jeffrey 
L. Seeman, CEP, on behalf of the Town Board, as well as Part 2, Part 3 and Part 3 
Continued Narrative of the FEAF dated March 18, 2025 prepared by Jeffrey L. Seeman, 
CEP, on behalf of the To wn Board; and as well as other relevant planning, zoning and 
environmental factors to date. Now, therefore, be it  
 
9.22
Packet Pg. 122
RESOLVED, that the Riverhead Town Board hereby assumes Lead Agency and 
issues a Negative Declaration pursuant to SEQRA, for the “Riverhead D owntown 
Revitalization” project as described herein above, as the proposed action is not 
expected to result in any significant adverse environmental impacts; and be it further 
 
RESOLVED, that the Riverhead Town Board directs the Planning Department on 
behalf of the Town board to submit said Negative Declaration to the New York State 
Department of Environmental Conservation (NYSDEC) Environmental Notice Bulletin 
(ENB); and be it further 
 
RESOLVED, that the Town Clerk is hereby authorized to forward a certifi ed copy 
of this resolution to the Planning Department, Community Development Department and 
the Town Attorney’s Office; and be it further 
  
RESOLVED, that all Town Hall Departments may review and obtain a copy of 
this resolution from the electronic storage device and if needed, a certified copy of same 
may be obtained from the Office of the Town Clerk. 
 
THE VOTE 
 
RESULT: ADOPTED [UNANIMOUS] 
MOVER: Robert Kern, Councilman

Page 1 of 10 
Full Environmental Assessment Form 
Part 2 - Identification of Potential Project Impacts 
Part 2 is to be completed by the lead agency.  Part 2 is designed to help the lead agency inventory all potential resources that could 
be affected by a proposed project or action.  We recognize that the lead agency=s reviewer(s) will not necessarily be environmental 
professionals.  So, the questions are designed to walk a reviewer through the assessment process by providing a series of questions that 
can be answered using the information found in Part 1.  To further assist the lead agency in completing Part 2, the form identifies the 
most relevant questions in Part 1 that will provide the information needed to answer the Part 2 question.  When Part 2 is completed, the 
lead agency will have identified the relevant environmental areas that may be impacted by the proposed activity.   
If the lead agency is a state agency and the action is in any Coastal Area, complete the Coastal Assessment Form before proceeding 
with this assessment. 
Tips for completing Part 2: 
• Review all of the information provided in Part 1.
• Review any application, maps, supporting materials and the Full EAF Workbook.
• Answer each of the 18 questions in Part 2.
• If you answer “Yes” to a numbered question, please complete all the questions that follow in that section.
• If you answer “No” to a numbered question, move on to the next numbered question.
• Check appropriate column to indicate the anticipated size of the impact.
• Proposed projects that would exceed a numeric threshold contained in a question should result in the reviewing agency
checking the box “Moderate to large impact may occur.”
• The reviewer is not expected to be an expert in environmental analysis.
• If you are not sure or undecided about the size of an impact, it may help to review the sub-questions for the general
question and consult the workbook.
• When answering a question consider all components of the proposed activity, that is, the Awhole action@.
• Consider the possibility for long-term and cumulative impacts as well as direct impacts.
• Answer the question in a reasonable manner considering the scale and context of the project.

Full Environmental Assessment Form 
Part 3 - Evaluation of the Magnitude and Importance of Project Impacts 
and  
Determination of Significance 
Part 3 provides the reasons in support of the determination of significance.  The lead agency must complete Part 3 for every question 
in Part 2 where the impact has been identified as potentially moderate to large or where there is a need to explain why a particular 
element of the proposed action will not, or may, result in a significant adverse environmental impact. 
Based on the analysis in Part 
3, the lead agency must decide whether to require an environmental impact statement to further assess 
the proposed action or whether available information is sufficient for the lead agency to conclude that the proposed action will not 
have a significant adverse environmental impact.  By completing the certification on the next page, the lead agency can complete its 
determination of significance. 
Reasons Supporting This Determination: 
To com
plete this section: 
• Identify the impact based on the Part 2 responses and describe its magnitude.  Magnitude considers factors such as severity,
size or extent of an impact.
• Assess th
e importance of the impact.  Importance relates to the geographic scope, duration, probability of the impact
occurring, number of people affected by the impact and any additional environmental consequences if the impact were to
occur.
• The as
sessment should take into consideration any design element or project changes.
• Repeat this process for each Part 2 question where the impact has been identified as potentially moderate to large or where
there is a need to explain why a particular element of the proposed action will not, or may, result in a significant adverse
environmental impact.
• Provide the reason(s) why the impact may, or will not, result in a significant adverse environmental impact
• For Conditional Negative Declarations identify the specific condition(s) imposed that will modify the proposed action so that
no significant adverse environmental impacts will result.
• Attach additional sheets, as needed.

Full Environmental Assessment Form 
Part 3- Evaluation of the Magnitude and Importance of Project Impacts and 
Determination of Significance 
(continued) 
Riverhead Downtown Revitalization 
March 18, 2025 
 
 
5. IMPACT OF FLOODING (continued): One primary objective of the Riverhead Downtown Revi talization 
plan is to address the long-term resiliency of the Peconic River waterfront properties. The existing surface 
parking fields, structures and properties on the south side of Main Street and part of the Proposed Action 
are located within the projected 2070 10-year flood elevation (9.01-ft. abmsl). T he elevations will be raised 
and terraced from an elevation of 14.25-ft. abmsl to existing elevations at Heidi Behr Way as mitigation 
against potential for continued flooding impacts. During the site development of 203/213 Main Street, an 
excess of +/ - 7,000 cubic yards of soil will be generated. This material  shall be sampled and analyzed 
pursuant to NYCRR Part 360.13 Special Requirements for Pre -Determined Beneficial Use of Fill Material  
subsection (e) and (f). The LVF Landscape Architects, PLLC preliminary/50% Design Development plans and 
cross-sections depict the proposed co ntours and spot elevati ons to achieve the flood mitigation within 
this Phase of the Town Square and Playground areas.       
 
9. IMPACT ON AESTHETIC RESOURCES: There will be a minor impact on existing view sheds associated with 
the existing parking fields, and specifically the parking field where the proposed First Street Parking Garage 
will be located. Observers located north of the proposed site and to the east at East Avenue will experience 
a change from the exiting views of the surface parking field . The architecture of the parking garage , the 
set back from adjoining properties and proposed landscaping must address the visual impacts of the 
garage and its potential as a local dominating structure. An option is to screen the building with adequate 
landscaping (of which there currently exists little to none) and require building facades that minimize visual 
impacts. The garage will also be designed with the standards and intent of the Downtown Pattern Book to 
the maximum extent practicable. One field observation noted the buildings located to the garage site’s 
north (along Second Street) have their rear yards abutting the First Street Parking Garage property, where 
the land has historically been used for parking. Once the parking garage is designed, the Town will further 
assess potential visual impact potential and determine what mitigation is required. As stated in the Part 1 
Narrative, the later Phased projects will require additional SEQRA level reviews to update temporal 
conditions and address specific impact potential once details of each of the future projects are refined.     
 
10. IMPACT ON HISTORIC  & ARCHEOLOGICAL RESOURCES : The Town of Riverhead has executed an 
agreement with the New York State Historic Preservation Office.  The agreement is included as Appendix 
10 of the FEAF Part 1 Narrative . The agreement serves to protect and mitigate potential for adverse 
impacts on historical and archeological resources. The existing buildings at the East End Arts , which are 
proposed for  relocation to higher elevations, will be further protected from potential flood damage. 
Relocated structures will also be  reinforced for structural inte grity and longevity. These preservations 
efforts will protect these cultural resources and are positive public benefits through implementation of 
the Proposed Action.      
 
11. IMPACT OF OPEN SPACE & RECREATION: Recreational resources and open space will not be adversely 
impacted by the Proposed Action. There will be a net increase in access and use in public space associated 
with the Upper and Lower Town Square, and the Amphitheater. The Adaptive Children’s Playground will 
9.22.b
Packet Pg. 187
Attachment: Combined FEAF Part 2 & 3 and Part 3 continuation  (2025-263 : Assumes Lead Agency & Issues Negative Declaration for TOR
 
2 
 
provide space for and use of recreational facilities for children who have or may have restrictions on using 
other Town recreational facilities.  These attributes of the Proposed Action are important benefits for child 
development.  
 
13. IMPACT OF TRANSPORTATION: The realignment of First Street and the First Street Parking Garage will 
alter the existing traffic patterns within the local downtown area. The First S treet improvements will 
provide a more define roadway connecting Roa noke Avenue at the west to East Avenue at its easterly 
terminus. East Street intersects Main Street (NYS 25) at its southerly terminus and this intersection is 
unsignalized and is controlled by a stop sign. East Avenue northbound intersects at Second Street (an east 
west local roadway). This intersection is controlled by stop signs. One block east of this intersection is 
Maple Avenue, a north/south local roadway that  intersects Main Street at the southerly terminus. The 
intersection of Maple Avenue and Main Street (NYS 25) is a signalized intersection.  It is recommended 
that the Town Board further assess how the proposed realignment and access to the parking garage may 
affect existing traffic patterns, and whether additional improvements would be necessary. Prior to  
finalizing the garage and First Street realignment Phase  a traffic impact study ( TIS) is recommended to 
assess potential impacts. The Preliminary Parking Program Plan included as supporting information depicts 
existing and future parking plans associated with implementing the Proposed Action. The magnitude of 
impact to transportation is assessed to be minor  because of several factors. The Proposed Action is 
planned as a “pedestrian friendly -walking downtown.” Although access to the downtown region as a 
destination may require vehicular use, with parking at the garage, once parked, the occupants are 
expected to walk, not drive through the downtown area. Street narrowing of Main Street and widening of 
the sidewalks with amenities will serve to slow vehicular speeds along Main Street, may deter vehicular 
use along NYS 25 and encourage greater pedestrian traffic, use of alternative transportation (public bus 
transportation, bicycle, Long Island Railroad).  
 
14. IMPACT ON ENERGY: There will be a minor impact on energy consumption. Electric and natural gas will 
be provided by PSEGLI and Key Span respectively. The Proposed Action will require utility improvements 
be placed underground. There will be minor disruption to the public and local businesses as the power 
utilizes together with sewer and water are placed underground. Repurposing the Science Museum Center 
and the proposed hotel/condominium project will require additional energy input. Energy conservation 
equipment and lighting will be implemented to minimize overall energy dem and. The impact on the 
existing energy supplies and providers generated by the Proposed Action approval is assessed to be of 
minor significance and magnitude.  
 
15. IMPACT ON NOISE, ODOR, & LIGHT: Noise generated by construction activities will increase above the 
ambient levels. The Town of Riverhead Town Code Chapter 251limits construction activities to the hours 
of 7:00 AM to 8:00 PM where noise levels are limited to below 65 dBA. Recent construction projects 
performed within the downtown area have generated noise and vibration impacts caused by impact pile 
installations. Alternati ve (helic al) pile and spread-footing foundation methods approvable by the 
Riverhead Building Department have proven to be a successful alternative and mitigation measure to avoid 
vibration and noise. The proposed hotel/condominium and repurposed Science Mu seum site 
developments will require foundation designs that avoid excessive vibration and noise during 
construction. Dust generated by construction will be controlled by routine “housekeeping” including daily 
sweeping and application of water during constr uction. Lighting impacts will be minimized by the 
implementation of the Town’s “dark sky” regulations that reduce backscatter by light shields, limits of pole 
heights and limits to luminescence.  The Proposed Action’s potential impacts on noise, odor and l ight is 
assessed as minimal and for the majority of impact potential only temporary due to project construction 
9.22.b
Packet Pg. 188
Attachment: Combined FEAF Part 2 & 3 and Part 3 continuation  (2025-263 : Assumes Lead Agency & Issues Negative Declaration for TOR
 
3 
 
periods. Construction staging plans and the phased approach of the Proposed Action will further minimize 
the potential for adverse impacts.  
 
16. IMPACT OF HUMAN HEALTH: An increase in solid and liquid waste generated by implementing the 
Downtown Revitalization projects is expected. There will be construction and demolition (C&D) generated 
by the short-term removal of exiting parking fields and cementitious structures. These C&D materials can 
be processed and an approved disposal facility and recycled and reused by the construction industry. An 
increase in municipal solid waste generated by the hotel/condominium, repurposed Science 
Center/Museum and the public’s use of the Town Square is expected to be limited in quantities (+/ -) 50 
tons/month. This quantity is the equivalent of two packer truckloads (typical garbage trucks have a 
capacity of 25 tons) per month. Wastewater will be conveyed via the  Riverhead Sewer District  (RSD) 
municipal sewer system and treated at the Riverhead Sewage Plant (STP) located east of the downtown 
region north of Riverside Drive. The RSD has been involved in the Downtown Revitalization planning 
process and the STP has the capacity to treat the additional wastewater generated by the Proposed Action. 
The potential for adverse impact on human health is small.  
  
Summary and Conclusions in Support of the Determination of Significance

Benefit Cost Analysis for Town Square and TOD - Dr. Martin R. Cantor, CPA (June 2021).

Draft/Final Environmental Impact Statement-203-213 East Main Street and SEQRA Findings Statement 
(2023-2024). 
Additionally, the design plans prepared to date for the initial Phases of the Proposed Action have been 
reviewed and evaluated for the SEQRA assessment.  
Flood attenuation, removal of blight within the Riverhead downtown designated Urban Renewal Area, and 
the public’s increased access to the riverfront are significant benefits. 
The Science Center/Museum structure is in violation of building codes. These violations have resulted in 
non-responsive actions by the owners .  The Town’s intent is to acqui re the site whereby the Town can  
proceed with the Downtown revitalization and flood mitigation efforts. The revitalization is compliant with 
urban renewal needs and is consistent with NYS Coastal Policies . The imp lementation of the Proposed 
Action will improve the quality of life in a proposed Enviro nmental Justice Area .  Therefore, there are 
strong social, safety, and economic benefits achieved by proceeding with the Proposed Action. There is 
also the practical importance of flood mitigation necessary to protect public and private pro perty and 
provide coastal resiliency of the downtown to address significant adverse impacts generated by major 
storm events, sea level rise, depth to groundwater which cause localized flooding.  
During the SEQRA review of the Phased development, no significant or moderate potential for adverse 
environmental impacts  have been  identified as significant in magnitude or importance to warrant 
justification of a Positive Declaration and require preparation of an Environmental Impact Statement.  
There are many public benefits that, pursuant to SEQRA environmental qualitative and quantitative 
assessment procedures, would qualify the proposed Action as having potential for impacts that could not 
be balanced, if not outweighed, by the public social and economic benefits.   
As quoted from the SEQRA Handbook, 4th edition,  
“It is not the intention of SEQR for environmental factors to be the sole consideration in agency 
decision-making. 
The purpose of SEQR is to ensure that the environmental impacts of an action are weighed and 
balanced with social, economic, and other considerations so that a suitable balance of social, 
economic, and environmental factors may be incorporated in the planning and decision-making 
processes of state, regional, and local agencies. 
How should an agency balance environmental harm against social and economic benefits in 
order to approve an action? 
SEQR gives considerable discretion to agencies to make decisions consistent with social, 
economic, and other essential considerations. This allows agencies to approve actions providing 
9.22.b
Packet Pg. 190
Attachment: Combined FEAF Part 2 & 3 and Part 3 continuation  (2025-263 : Assumes Lead Agency & Issues Negative Declaration for TOR
 
5 
 
social or economic benefits even if all environmental impacts cannot be totally avoided or 
mitigated. However, the underlying requirements that adverse environmental impacts must be 
avoided or minimized, and mitigation measures applied remain. Thus, the more a project fulfills 
needs and provides important, public, social, and economic benefits, the more an agency may 
conclude that it can accept certain adverse environmental impacts.” 
Based on the above statement, the Proposed Action is consistent with the spirit and intent of the State 
Environmental Quality Review Act.  Furthermore, the completion of the FEAF  Part 2  has n ot revealed 
substantive adverse environmental impacts that cannot be avoided or minimized by adhering to standard 
Riverhead Town Code requirements and site plan procedures. These include the preparation of a Traffic 
Impact Study to further review potential changes to existing traffic patterns resulting from the First Street 
and First Street Garage construction project, and infrastructure improvements as warranted by the RSD 
and RWD. Strict coordination during the physical construction and its planning are necessary to avoid and 
minimize nuisance impacts associated with projects constructed in an existing urbanized and developed 
area located adjacent to the Peconic River and estuary.        
Because the Action requires multiple phases and individual project designs are in different stages of 
completion, impact potential variables are currently unknown. For consistency with SEQRA, the following 
Standards will be applied as methods to avoid, min imize and mitigate moderate to significant impact 
potential.  
DOWNTOWN REVITALIZATION: MITIGATION STANDARDS 
1. Individual projects shall be subject to further SEQRA review for compliance with the Narrative 
and Standards set forth herein.  The Lead Agency has a ttempted to assess the potential for 
impacts, based upon the available information for the multi -phased Proposed Action. 
Pursuant to SEQRA, t here are special circumstances where a segmented review is justified  
provided the Determination of Significance pro vides clear reasons and demonstrates the 
segmented review will be no less protective of the environment. Such conditions are 
applicable to multi -phased projects  involving various stages of development, funding and 
review.  
 
The Lead Agency finds these circumstances applicable to the Downtown Revitalization project. 
Some of the i ndividual projects that comprise the Proposed Action have not been advanced 
to equal stages of engineering and architectural designs, and/or are incomplete with respect 
to site controls or fund ing sources. The development of the First Street Parking Garage and 
street improvements are in a conceptual phase and require additional review. Other projects 
located on the south side of Main Street including raising the elevations and development of 
the Upper and Lower Town Square, Amphitheater, the acquisition of the Science Center site, 
have been advanced to the degree where assessment for adverse impacts have been clarified, 
can be avoided and/or mitigated to the maximum extent practicable. 
 
The Lead Agency determined the SEQRA review of the Proposed Action as the “Whole Action” 
is necessary to advance the Action toward additional phases involving more detailed planning, 
environmental review and funding.  The Lead Agency is cognizant of its responsibility to 
evaluate the Whole Action irrespective of individual project design stages. The Lead Agency 
9.22.b
Packet Pg. 191
Attachment: Combined FEAF Part 2 & 3 and Part 3 continuation  (2025-263 : Assumes Lead Agency & Issues Negative Declaration for TOR
 
6 
 
finds that  a second “hard look” of  several individual projects is necessary to support the 
findings determined pursuant to this FEAF and Determination of Significance. 
 
This second environmental assessment will be conducted during the site planning process to 
assure the projects follow these findings or if additional mitigating measures are warranted. 
Projects excluded from these additional environmental reviews are the Upper and Lower Town 
Square, the Amphitheater, the Rowing Facility, improvements for traffic calming along Main 
Street, the acquisition and demolition of the Science Center site. 
 
The relocation of the East End Arts Buildings with grade adjustments necessary to raise the  
site’s elevation, proposed the First Street Parking Garage and roadway/parking field 
realignment, the Railroad Avenue Overl ay District developments will require additional 
assessments. The proposed hotel and condominium have undergone environmental reviews 
as part of this EAF and will be subject to additional reviews for compliance with these findings 
upon site plan submission to the Town of Riverhead. 
 
Proposed redevelopment of the Science Center site will also require detailed environmental 
assessment be conducted. Currently no proposed uses of the Science Center sit e are 
envisioned. A theoretical scenario similar to the proposed hotel and condominium site was 
used to evaluate potential impacts. The existing conditions of the Science Center building is 
not safe or habitable, is within the flood zone and will be subjec ted to demolition after it is 
acquired.     
2. Project designs and implementation shall follow the Downtown Riverhead Pattern Book (UDA, 
January 2021). (FinalPatternBook2021 -01-141505092833011421AM.pdf 
(townofriverheadny.gov) 
3. The Fire Access Plan shall not be modified or obstructed unless authorized by the Town of 
Riverhead Fire Marshal. 
4. All projects located along the south side of Main Street shall comply with the Flood Mitigation 
Design and Construction requirements as specified by the Town of Riverhead. 
5. Projects are subject to further Traffic Impact assessment as may be determined by the Town 
of Riverhead environmental review process as specified in item 1 of these Standards.  
6. Infrastructure improvements (including but not limited to, signalized and unsign alized 
intersections, water mains, sanitary sewers, stormwater controls, etc.) shall be determined 
during the Town of Riverhead site plan and environmental review process, with infrastructure 
improvement costs subject to standard conditions set forth under  the standard site plan 
review procedures and requirements. (Riverhead Town Code: Chapter 301 Zoning and Land 
Development). 
7. Landscaping and Stormwater Management Systems shall incorporate bio -engineering 
principals to mitigate potential urban pollution (ra in gardens, bio -swales, Mayawaki Forest, 
etc.) and include formal landscape and stormwater management maintenance plans as 
specified by the Town of Riverhead Town Engineering and Planning Departments. 
8. The p roject sponsors shall prepare and be subjected to approvable detailed construction 
planning and staging plans. Plans shall address material storage, employee parking, traffic and 
parking controls necessary to minimize disruption to local downtown business operations, and

the public. Approved plans shall b e subjected to continuous monitoring by the Town of

Enhanced Streetscapes and Public Gathering Places Creating a New Town Square - DRI Award: 
$3,240,000 
• Build a new public plaza and gathering space that can facilitate year-round 
activation and provide accessible pedestrian connections and vistas from Main 
Street to the riverfront. 
• Enhancing Peconic Park with an Adaptive Playground - DRI Award: $245,000 
Construct a playground and park space with a water feature and educational 
activities that relate to the waterfront location and utilize green infrastructure 
and design to aid downtown resiliency efforts. 
• Enhancing the Pedestrian Realm Along Main Street - DRI Award: $750,000 
Install traffic calming design elements to improve pedestrian safety along Main 
Street at two prominent intersections, including curb bump-outs, raised 
crosswalks. and pedestrian signalization. Install new street trees and landscaping. 
• Building a New Town Rowing Facility - DRI Award: $250,000 
Construct a floating ADA accessible community boat launch facility in the Peconic 
River with space to maneuver and launch crew boats and, if feasible, racks to store 
the crew boats. 
• Expanded Arts and Cultural Activity Implementing Public Art Program - DRI Award: $250,000 
Engage local artists to build permanent public artworks in Downtown Riverhead, 
building on success of existing community artworks. 
• Expanding the Suffolk Theater - DRI Award: $2,000,000 
Expand an existing, historic theater stage and add green room and back of house 
functions, all as a component of a larger development with residential units that 
include workforce housing. 
• Building a New Entrance and Welcome Center for the Library - DRI Award: 
$215,000 
Provide a new accessible entrance and pedestrian path with signage, lighting and 
landscaping and include interior space for a self-serving visitor center providing 
promotional materials for Downtown businesses and events. 
• Increased Housing and Business Opportunities 
Creating a Mixed-Use Development at Griffing Avenue - DRI Award: $2,750,000 
Construct a new mixed-use development consisting of workforce housing and 
retail/commercial space lining a public parking structure.

The Riverhead Town Board, as SEQRA Lead Agency, has reviewed the Full Environmental Assessment 
Forms Parts 1, 2 and 3 together with supporting documents and public comments received during the 
SEQRA review period. 
 
The Lead Agency has reviewed the implementation of Riverhead Downtown Revitalization Phased Urban 
Renewal Project  and determined the Proposed Action  will not result in  significant potential adverse 
environmental impacts. The Lead Agency has weighed and balanced the potential for adverse impacts 
with social, economic, and other considerations. 
 
The Lead Agency asserts a suitable balance of social, economic, and environmental factors can and has 
been incorporated into the planning and its decision-making processes. 
 
The Lead Agency has coordinated the SEQRA review with state, regional, local agencies and interested 
parties, and has received comments, which have been addressed and made part of the SEQRA record. 
 
Furthermore, The Proposed Action occurs within the designated  “Riverhead Downtown Urban Renewal 
Area,” where the Town Board asserts authority for: site plan review and approval; is the governing body 
of the  Riverhead Downtown Parking District ; are Commissioners of  the Riverhead  Water District; are 
Commissioners of the Riverhead Sewer District; are board members of the Town of Riverhead Community 
Development Agency; are among the property owners where the Action is proposed; and are the SEQRA 
Lead Agency and sponsor of the Proposed Action. 
 
The Town Board shall maintain its authority over the Proposed Action, such as additional environmental 
review(s), as needed and conducted during the Proposed Action ’s future phases(s) or unforeseen 
environmental impact potential segmented from this FEAF shall be avoided or mitigated to the maximum 
extent practicable. 
 
 
 
 
 
 
The Town of Riverhead Town Board, as Lead Agency, hereby designates the Proposed Action a Negative 
Declaration of Significance.

Town of Riverhead  Full Environmental Assessment Form : Downto wn Revitalization  Project : 
March 2025  
Response to Comments  
 
The Town of Riverhead posted the FEAF Part 1 and Part 1 Narrative Statement with appendix on the Town’s 
website on January 3, 2025. The Town Board received two written letters expressing comments about the 
proposed action. 
Wayne Steck, submitted comments on Summer Wind letterhead, dated January 16, 2025, as “Eastern 
Properties Investment Consultants.”  The comments included concerns about homeless people, crime, public 
safety, waterfront visibility and support for local businesses.  
As a general response to Mr. Steck, the Town Board acknowledges that the public’s input acquired during 
the Pattern Book development, the Town Square process and the adopted zoning, were specifically directed 
to address these concerns. The purpose of the revitalization program is to address these issues within the 
downtown Urban Renewal Area. The Upper and Lower Town Square, amphitheater, hotel/condominium. 
East End Arts building relocation, First Street Parking Garage (including the Riverhead Town Police Sub-
station and street realignment are intended to attract larger public use of the downtown area, which will 
increase access to the riverfront, local businesses, which will also improve overall public safety through 
police and the public’s presence. 
The second letter received from Mr. Steck, dated January 16, 2025, and published on “The Landmark of 
Riverhead”-103/105 East Main Street letterhead and as property owner and investor/developer in Riverhead. 
One concern was for a seven-foot wall; and a second was for “a rising tide.” The letter advocated for 
increasing foot traffic, public involvement with the redevelopment of the downtown, and incentives for 
property owners to beautify their facades and flood protection. In response, the Town Board has offered 
extensive opportunities for the public and local downtown business and property owners to participate in 
the planning and development process. These opportunities included the East Main Street Urban Renewal 
Area (EMSURA) and Brownfield programs, public hearing on proposed zone changes, public comments to 
the Updated Comprehensive Plan, public input for the Pattern Book and Town Square development 
programs.  
The Town of Riverhead Parking District Advisory Committee submitted comments by letter dated January 
6, 2025. The following are the responses to those comments: 
Procedural  
Comment 1: Involved Agency Status 
Response: 
Pursuant to 6CRR-NY Part 617.2 Definitions (t) Involved agency means an agency that has jurisdiction by 
law to fund, approve or directly undertake and action, If an agency will ultimately make a discretionary 
decision to fund, approve or undertake an action, then it is an “involved agency” notwithstanding that it has 
not received an application for funding or approval at the time the SEQR process is commenced. The “lead 
agency” is also an involved agency.” 
Pursuant to 6CRR-NY Part 617.2 Definitions (u): Interested agency means an agency that lacks the 
jurisdiction to fund, approve, or directly undertake an action but wishes to participate in the review process 
because of specific expertise or concern about the proposed action. An “interested agency” has the same 
ability to participate in the review process as a member of the public. 
The Town of Riverhead Parking District Advisory Committee does not meet the legal standards of an 
involved agency because the committee per sea cannot fund, approve or undertake the proposed Town of 
Riverhead Revitalization (the Whole Action). The approval authority such as issuance of permits, funding, 
and similar discretionary decisions is not within the advisory committee’s legal responsibility. As an 
9.22.c
Packet Pg. 199
Attachment: Part 3 Attachments  (2025-263 : Assumes Lead Agency & Issues Negative Declaration for TOR Downtown Revitalization Projects)
 
advisory committee, the specific area of interest and expertise is limited to parking and parking district 
concerns. The Riverhead Town Board is the governing body of the Town of Riverhead Parking District and 
has jurisdiction by law, to fund, approve and undertake actions that are within the parking district 
boundaries. The statement suggesting that the Town Board represents the taxpayers within the parking 
district, as separate and autonomous to the “entirety of town taxpayers” is contradictory. The taxpayers 
within the parking district are also included within the “entirety of town taxpayer,” in the same way as 
taxpayers within the sewer district, water district and all special districts are members of townwide 
taxpayers.     
Furthermore, as the sponsor of the Downtown Revitalization Program, the Town Board has quasi 
discretionary decision making and funding responsibilities. The Town Board is responsible for:  
-Governing site plan review within the Riverhead Town designated Urban Renewal Areas 
-Lead Agency under the SEQRA review and procedures 
-Approval of financial assistance and fiducial responsibility for financial obligations committed to the action 
-Governing the Riverhead Sewer District  
-Governing the Riverhead Water District 
-Governing the Town of Riverhead Community Development Agency 
Comment 2: Town Board Lead Agency Request Resolution and Potential Fiscal Impact 
Response: 
Resolution 2024-982 is a request for Lead Agency designation necessary for SEQRA Type 1 procedural 
actions. This request is required simply for beginning the SEQRA process, and for the required coordinated 
review. There are no financial impacts associated with this step of the SEQRA process.   
Comment 3: Date of FEAF Part 1 and Resolution for Lead Agency 
Response: 
A request for Lead Agency can begin at the earliest opportunity, and upon recognition that a Type One 
action will require coordinated review among involved agencies. The selection of a lead agency must take 
place within 30 days of the initial request. If the request is challenged, the timeframe is stopped until the 
involved agencies agree on suitability of the lead agency, or the Commissioner of the NYSDEC determines 
the most appropriate agency to be the lead agency. Likewise, Part One Full Environmental Assessment Form 
is initiated upon initiation of the action. Signatories and dates on the FEAF and narrative are completed after 
the resolution is passed. There is no concern about procedural error. The formal circulation of the lead 
agency request is dated January 3, 2025; and the deadline for response is February 3. 2025.  
Parking District Properties 
Comment 1: Location of Proposed Action and site control 
A review of the portion of the Parking District located at the southwest corner of the East End Arts parcel 
indicated that a maximum of four (4) parking stalls will be removed. The loss of four stalls has only a minor 
impact. These four stalls will likely to be accommodated elsewhere within the district or a dedication of four 
stalls located within a parking field owned by the Town of Riverhead may be an option. When analyzed for 
the benefits generated by replacing the existing four stalls with the proposed amphitheater and increasing 
the elevations of the East End Arts site, how these combined developments are critical for flood attenuation, 
the minor impact to parking is significantly outweighed by the proposed action. 
Comment 2: Annexation of Parking District property and Parking District fiduciary responsibility  
9.22.c
Packet Pg. 200
Attachment: Part 3 Attachments  (2025-263 : Assumes Lead Agency & Issues Negative Declaration for TOR Downtown Revitalization Projects)
 
Response: 
The annexation of Parking District properties can be executed by the Town of Riverhead Town Attorney’s 
Office at the appropriate time, such as prior to actual construction. The Town Board as governing body of 
the Parking District can initiate the action.  The outstanding bond debt is, and has always been, the 
responsibility of the Town Board as governing body of the Riverhead Parking District. The debt can be 
reduced or extinguished through a variety of financial options such as use of parking district fund balance. 
Again, the Town Board is fully aware of the financial commitments of the Parking District, but it is 
premature to act upon selecting a particular path of action until a full scope of capital investment is better 
defined and funding options, including additional grant approvals, are finalized.    
Coordinated Parking Plan  
Comment 1: Parking District request for coordinated parking plan. 
Response: 
As stated in the FEAF Narrative, a construction coordination plan will be developed for each Phase of the 
development. Construction staging plans will identify material storage areas, construction employee 
parking areas, and public parking areas, Recent large-scale developments that occurred on the south side 
of East Main Street have required construction staging plans. Proposed construction for the 203-213 
mixed use development is also required to submit an approvable construction staging plan. The proposed 
action will involve a comprehensive construction coordinated program, specific to each Phase and with 
consideration to ongoing private development, with the least impact upon the public and the Parking 
District as is practicable. There will be temporary disruption during the project development. Advance 
notice and signage for areas where the public can park will be included with the coordinated 
construction planning.      
Comment 2: Request to add Parking Program Plan prepared by Level G Associates. 
Response: 
The Preliminary Parking Program Plan is added (attachment-1). As projects phased in, parking 
accommodations will be defined in the construction staging plans.  
Comment 3: Concerns about a net loss of 17 parking spaces due to hotel and other development. 
Response: 
There is some speculation to the comment. There is no “lease” arrangement for the use of parking spaces, and 
the hotel occupancy rate is a dynamic and variable condition. There is expected to be flexibility in parking 
areas designated for the public and for the proposed development. The Parking District area parking stalls 
are not 100% utilized 100% of each day, each year. If there were a loss of parking stalls resulting in significant 
impacts to the Parking District the Town of Riverhead will explore options to make up the difference by 
accommodating the taxing District. This could be by providing additional parking on Town of Riverhead 
properties. As the Town Board is the governing body of the Parking District it has the internal authority to 
provide such an arrangement. The Town Board will seek advice from the Committee and the public when 
and if a net loss in parking stalls is a significant issue. The need for redevelopment and ability to revitalize 
the blighted areas within the downtown Urban Renewal Area is critical for the commercial businesses and 
residents of Riverhead. After a decade of planning and public participation, if the proposed Action results in 
a loss of 17 stalls, the public social and economic benefits resulting from the Action are expected to outweigh 
the potential impact of a net loss of 17 parking stalls. However, there are options that will be explored as 
more refined engineering and planning for future phases of the project are scheduled.  
Comments 3 & 4: Loss of parking areas due to Fire Access configuration, and development proposed on 
existing parking areas. 
9.22.c
Packet Pg. 201
Attachment: Part 3 Attachments  (2025-263 : Assumes Lead Agency & Issues Negative Declaration for TOR Downtown Revitalization Projects)
 
Response: 
The proposed action does not include the referenced site depicted on the Level G Associates 
parking program as “potential future development.” There is no Proposed development planned 
for the location to the west of East Avenue. Furthermore, the Town Board has determined the site 
is not an appropriate location for additional future development. The existing parking stalls will 
remain and not be impacted by the proposed action. 
 
The Fire Access as configured is necessary for public safety and emergency response.   
 
 
The Parking Garage at First Street 
 
Comments 1 & 2  Concerns for ownership and fees:    
 
Response:  
The response to item 1 has been provided under “Parking District Properties.” In response to Item 2; there 
have been no decisions regarding ownership, operating procedures, and parking fees. The SEQRA Narrative 
clearly outlined the Phased development strategies necessary because each proposed project is in different 
stages of design. 
 
The First Street Parking Garage design has not been developed to a stage where these decisions can be made. 
What is relevant is that all the phases are being reviewed under this assessment, and each is subject to an 
additional environmental assessment to further address potential impact thresholds and mitigating measures 
as may be necessary. Operations, maintenance, use of the garage, and resident parking requirements are not 
within the scope of the assessment currently. 
 
 The Town Board, as the governing body of the Parking District and SEQRA Lead Agency will continue to 
engage the Parking District Advisory Committee and other interested parties to seek comments and 
recommendations for the First Street Parking Garage. 
 
The Town Board will be responsible for all decisions regarding ownership, operations and fees associated 
with the First Street Parking Garage.   
  
Comment 3: Concern for potential traffic impacts: 
 
Response: 
 
The Town Board, as part of the SEQRA process and its request for Lead Agency, has circulated 
the FEAF Part 1 and Narrative to involved agencies including the NYS Department of 
Transportation. Once the Town Board is designated as Lead Agency it will review comments 
received regarding traffic impact potential and as warranted, address the concerns through a 
Traffic Impact Study (TIS). This is a standard function for many applications requiring Town of 
Riverhead Planning Department, Engineering Department and inter-agency reviews. The First 
Street Parking Garage and the other proposed revitalization projects will be subjected to the 
standard site plan and engineering reviews like other Town of Riverhead applications. At the 
appropriate stage and as warranted during the review process, the TIS will be prepared.

03.18.2025 ADOPTED 
 
 
TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
 
TB Resolution 2025-264 
 
GRANTS CHAPTER 229 EXCAVATION/EXPORTATION PERMIT FOR FISHER 
ORGANIZATION LLC 836 E MAIN STREET RIVERHEAD NY  SCTM NO. 600-127-6-
07.1 
 
Councilwoman Merrifield offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilwoman Waski 
 
WHEREAS, the Planning Board, by Resolution No. 2024-042, dated June 6, 
2024, granted approval for the site plan application of 836 E Main Street Mixed Use 
Building (Fisher Organization), to permit the construction of a 13,083 sq.ft. Two-story 
mixed-use building consisting of eight (8) residential apartments on upper floors, (6 two-
bedroom units, 2 one-bedroom units) 6,558 sq.ft. of ground floor commercial space 
along with related site improvements and 2,641 sq. ft. basement and 2996 sq. Ft. crawl 
space, upon real property located at 836 E Main Street Riverhead, NY, more particularly 
described as SCTM No. 600-127-6-7.1; and  
 
WHEREAS, Fisher Organization, LLC, has submitted a Chapter 229 
Excavation/Exportation permit to allow for the excavation and exportation of 2,851 cubic 
yards of earthen material from this parcel; and  
 
WHEREAS, the Building Department is in receipt of an earthwork plan, signed 
and sealed by Martin F. Sendlewski, last dated August, 9, 2024, in accordance with the 
approved site plan; and  
 
WHEREAS, the Town Board has reviewed and considered the application for the 
aforementioned excavation/exportation permit.  Now, therefore be it 
 
RESOLVED, that based upon the forgoing, the Town Board hereby grants the 
Chapter 229 Excavation/Exportation permit requested by the application, to authorize 
the excavation and exportation of 2,851 cubic yards of material in accordance with the 
approved site plan and earthwork calculations aforementioned; and be it further 
 
RESOLVED, the Building Department is hereby authorized to accept and collect 
a permit fee of $5,902.00; representing $2.00 per cubic yard for the exportation of said 
soils, in addition to a permit fee of $100.00; and be it further  
 
RESOLVED, that the Town Clerk is hereby authorized to send a certified copy of 
this resolution to the Building Department, the Planning Department; and be it further 
 
RESOLVED, that all Town Hall Departments may obtain a copy of this resolution 
from the electronic storage device; and be it further 
 
RESOLVED, that a certified copy of this resolution may be obtained from the 
Town Clerk’s office by request.

NOTICE TO BIDDERS 
 
 
Sealed bids for DRY HYDRATED LIME (CALCIUM HYDROXIDE) will be received by the 
Town Clerk of the Town of Riverhead at Town Hall, 4 W 2nd Street, Riverhead, New York, 
11901, until 11:00 a.m. on April 3, 2025, at which time all bids received shall be opened
